B0087UN94E|3.0|Hours after Neil Young and his new bandmates (CS&N) left the stage at Woodstock in 1969, Jimi Hendrix closed out that historic concert with his smoldering rendition of the national anthem. Neil later paid homage to Jimi with his grunge version of \\"Where the Buffalo Roam,\\" in the movie of the same title, that featured Bill Murray doing a (pre-Johnny Depp) imitation of Hunter Thompson. Like Jimi's \\"Anthem,\\" Neil's was a reimagining of a familiar American folk song that pulled it up by the roots that gave it contemporary meaning. (Perhaps this is why Sha Na Na, who played in between CSN&Y and Jimi that day, is referenced here with \\"Get A Job,\\" the least congruous tune on this disc--it have fit in better on his \\"Neil and the Shocking Pinks\\" CD). Neil periodically revisits his roots, often by getting \\"back to the country,\\" covering classics like \\"Oh, Lonesome Me,\\" \\"Four Strong Winds\\" and \\"The Wayward Wind.\\" On this album, he reminds us of those lyrics on his solo debut--\\"I used to be a folksinger...\\"<br /><br />Although some may be disappointed by the fact there are no new Neil compositions on this record, it is good to see him get back on the Horse again and behold them riding in all their ragged glory. One of my favorite live NY shows of all time was Neil and Crazy Horse \\"In a Rusted Out Garage\\" at San Fransico's Cow Palace in 1986. Perhaps they will hook a whole new generation of fans when they headline Outside Lands in Golden Gate Park this summer. Yet I suspect most of the people who purchase this record now will be fans already, especially guitarists anxious to hear what Neil does tearing through these familiar tunes in his unique style. Like other Neil/Horse collaborations, grunge tends to dominate here--only \\"Wayfarin' Stranger\\" is given the acoustic treatment. The disc is topped off by the transplanted Candadian's grunge tribute to the queen. This brings us full circle back to 1969--the same year Jimi closed out Woodstock with his Anthem, the Beatle's closed outAbbey Road with \\"Her Majesty.\\" Neil's homage to HRH would fit in well on the set-list of those UK punk bands that would re-energize rock and roll after the Woodstock flame had dimmed.<br /><br />I gave this CD 3 stars because it is a middling effort by Neil, but is still better than much of what passes for music these days. I was reminded of a few other \\"back to the roots\\" efforts by rockers from Neil's era, such as Eric Clapton's Robert Johnson tribute CD. And both Neil and Clapton played at \\"Bobfest,\\" where various artists from the many traditions that influenced (and who were influenced BY) Dylan gathered to honor him. But the closest analogy seems to be the 2008 effort by fellow Bay Area icon Paul Kantner, who assembled members of the Jefferson<br />Airplane/Starship cast to update and rework traditional folk songs on \\"Jefferson's Tree of Liberty.\\" That work, as Neil's newest is likely to become, was \\"polarizing\\" for fans--while some saw it as a solid effort to revisit the roots, others viewed it as mere \\"coasting\\" in the absence of new material. But artists like Neil, Dylan, the Airplane and the Dead owed much to traditional folk music like that presented on \\"Americana.\\"

However, I think the book could have been written better. It gets too wordy at times with too many details that I don't find of interest. Yes, I love having an image in my head of a scene, but sometimes Stieg Larsson's descriptions end up boring me instead of fascinating me. He also puts in many details about government and politics, but that part is understandable. The trilogy is thrilling and action-packed, but it is also a portrayal of corruption and how secrets in government end up harming the citizens the government is supposed to protect.<br /><br />Lisbeth is an amazing character and I guess part of the reason I like her so much is that it's unlikely there's any real person like her out in the world. It's rare that a main character who is so antisocial, socially awkward, and so distant is so likable. You end up cheering her on and supporting her acts of violence because all her life, she has been mistreated and misunderstood. You want her to get her justice. And of course, she gets it done Lisbeth Salander-style. You can't trust the government to properly deliver justice in this case because the leaders in government don't even fully know what's going on.<br /><br />All in all, this is a great trilogy that combines action, crazy characters, and politics. It's a crazy mix but it works.

I'm going to go out limb here and boast getting just about every 80s pop culture reference in this novel, but even more scary, all of the nerd computer, gaming (role-playing) and video game reference as well.  In other words, I get it... deeply.  And I loved it.  Never before has a movie or book brought back so much fond nostalgia for me, and Ernest Cline absolutely nailed it.  I guessing he and I could trade stories over an afternoon and come away thinking we shared the same childhood in alternate, parallel universes, and in that regard Ready Player One is 5-stars worth of fun.<br /><br />Unfortunately, if you don't happen to be a mid-80s alumni who majored in Nerdery, I can't recommend this book because while it's great nostalgia, it's mediocre science fiction at best.  Ironically, while I imagine its most enthusiastic audience will be males 35-45, in many ways Ready Player One reminded me of YA fiction.  The relationships between the main characters are simplistic and juvenile.  Some dire, real-world events are brought up, twice, but the reactions to them are shallow.  In one case (no spoiler), the reaction is essentially \\"sure they died, but they sucked so who cares\\".  In the other case, the reaction is essentially \\"I will avenge you!\\" and that's pretty much it.  The game itself has no consequences aside from you having to roll up a new level 1 toon, so unlike The Matrix, one never feels overly concerned for the \\"heroes\\" and what's going on with them in their virtual world.  So, what's the hook?  Why are we to be concerned if the hero doesn't prevail?  Well, you basically have to get invested in the idea that if the \\"bad guys\\" win, the MMORPG everyone in the world loves will become more commercialized.  Umm... ok... I guess that's bad... ish.<br /><br />So, for me, Ready Player One was a glorious, 6 hour read down Memory Lane.  For most people, however, I think it's going to be a simplistic story about some kid you'll like (when he's not being a dick because he's a kid) against some gamer CEO who's a dick because he's the big, bad businessman who doesn't care if he cheats and kills people.  You will proceed along the plot of this story in a linear, no surprises fashion.  You will never be in doubt how this story will end.  You will not fear for the protagonists.  You will not be challenged to imagine the consequences to humanity of an immersive virtual \\"game\\" played by essentially everyone.  You will get Schoolhouse Rock tunes stuck in your head.<br /><br />I toyed with giving a 2-star review, but decided that wasn't fair.  I did enjoy Ready Player One, and I think people who aren't too demanding of their scifi entertainment will think \\"it's OK\\"... which is the definition of 3-stars according to the rating tool.  Do not, however, come to this book with 5-star expectations because once you discard all the 80s trivia, there's not a whole lot left to recommend.oll up a new level 1 toon, so unlike The Matrix, one never feels overly concerned for the \\"heroes\\" and what's going on with them in their virtual world. B007RKPO84|5.0|Kreator have been on a real upward trajectory artistically speaking for the last decade or so. Since 2001's superb Violent Revolution album and the establishment of their current line-up, everything that the band have put out has been of the utmost quality, keeping to a fairly strict but non-intrusive formula and just knocking out a boatload of brilliant songs.<br /><br />Now in 2012, with their thirteenth full-length studio album Phantom Antichrist, the legendary German Thrash Metal band continue in the same vein that has kept the last three albums so absolutely vital and deliver more of the same formula that mixes their classic 1980s style with elements of Gothenburg style, an intermittent touch of groove and a few sections with clean vocals over arpeggiated bits in their too for variety.<br /><br />Each of the albums that follow that aforementioned formula also puts enough of an individual twist on it to have its own identity though, and I guess Phantom Antichrist's twist would be that it isn't just as fast, isn't just as heavy as often and is a lot more focused on the high-end. It's a more melodic and musical take of the Enemy Of God/Hordes Of Chaos musical direction.<br /><br />Despite the title track leading with speed and low end, there's a lot of time given on the album overall to slow sections, little guitar vibratos, teasing rolls or little sneaky Hi-Hat strikes. If you are all about the Thrash side of things don't worry though, it isn't as if the band abandoned Thrash, there is a heck of a lot of it in there too. The band did a clever job of balancing mixing things up with keeping what was working well.<br /><br />I have nothing but praise for this album, on first listen it already gave off \\"Album Of The Year Candidate\\" feelings and still grew on me with each subsequent spin. The performance is so energetic and pounding on the heavier songs and so subtle and studied on the more musical moments, the production is absolutely top-rate, Mille's vocals are up to the same standard of the recent few albums and the lead guitar work is inspired as always. Furthermore it is a pretty perfect length and each individual song is excellent so there is nothing in the way of filler. The album is lean, varied and perfectly formed.<br /><br />If this happened to be the first Kreator album that you ever heard I am sure it would leave a damn fine first impression. If you are an existing fan it is definitely more of the same flawless formula that has been working so well on one hand, and yet also a bit of a surprise at the same time, which just helps make it fresh and worthwhile.<br /><br />Highlights include the superb `Death To The World,' which has some brilliant lead guitar work and a surprising mid-section, the proggy closer `Until Our Paths Cross Again' as well as the groovy and complex `The Few The Proud The Broken' and which is exemplary of a few tracks on the album that take some of the spirit of Power Metal festival-pleasing choruses but applies it to a mostly mid-tempo Thrash number.<br /><br />Overall, this is a really great album from a truly consistent and focused band that know how to write good metal songs. The only thing which I could imagine anyone ever finding bad about this album would be the idea of the band repeating themselves, for example there is a riff in `Civilizations Collapse' that sounds like one in `Coma Of Souls' and one in `United In Hate' that sounds like one in `Replicas Of Life' etc but the band pull it off so well it doesn't bother me personally. If you usually find riff-recycling a massive pain then maybe the album won't seem just as flawless as I make it out to be, so that is something to take into consideration.<br /><br />As long as you liked the past few Kreator albums and aren't either sick of them or shocked at something that isn't exactly as heavy as their last two albums even if it makes up for it in other areas however, then Phantom Antichrist should be a no-brainer love affair right from the get-go.<br /><br />In summary; If you want some perfectly crafted German Metal, with absolutely superb lead guitar work, great drum work and the occasional moments of sing-along grandeur or softer moments brushing shoulders with pounding yet intelligent and varied Thrash, then this is certainly worth picking up.<br /><br />*** If you should happen to buy the Special Edition version, you will get one card-sleeve housing two individual digipak cases. The first has the actual album and the second has the bonus DVD.<br /><br />The DVD features a twenty-minute making-of documentary called `Conquerers Of The Ice.' Although it is a making-of there isn't that much in-studio footage, maybe around a total of three minutes. The bulk of the feature is three separate interviews that are cut together with studio footage between cuts. The producer Jens Borgen is interviewed at Fascination Street Studios where the album was recorded, and Mille Petrozza is interviewed on a frozen Ocean, while guitarist Sami Yli-Sirni&ouml; is interviewed in front of a Swedish castle. Topics covered include recording in Sweden, avoiding cheesiness, Osama Bin-Laden's death, the Greek economy and simultaneously tracking all members at once while recording. It isn't the most substantial documentary in the world, but it is a lot better than the one from Hordes Of Chaos.<br /><br />The DVD also features a live concert from Waken Open Air Festival 2011, intercut with four tracks from Waken 2006, but done in a way that you mightn't even notice if it wasn't pointed out to you. This isn't just the live-feed slapped onto a disc however, the footage and sound have been treated, edited and tidied up and it is actually a really good feature. It may cut to the monitors a little too often and not feature all that much off of their 80s albums, but it is a damn fine live show nonetheless.<br /><br />The tracklisting is:<br />1. (Intro) Choir Of The Damned<br />2. Hordes Of Chaos<br />3. War Curse<br />4. Endless Pain (with a riff from Coma Of Souls as an intro)<br />5. Pleasure To Kill<br />6. Destroy What Destroys You<br />7. (Intro) The Patriarch<br />8. Violent Revolution<br />9. People Of The Lie<br />10. Europe After The Rain<br />11. Phobia<br />12. Reconquering The Throne (with a riff from Terrible Certainty as an intro)<br />13. Flag of Hate/Tormentor<br /><br />The concert lasts 53.50 and with the improved visuals is probably actually a better DVD than their Live Kreation Revisioned Glory release. I highly recommend getting this bonus version if you can get it for cheap enough and as long as you enjoyed the Hordes Of Chaos album that makes up a lot of its track listing.  ***e get-go.<br /><br />In summary; If you want some perfectly crafted German Metal, with absolutely superb lead guitar work, great drum work and the occasional moments of sing-along grandeur or softer moments brushing shoulders with pounding yet intelligent and varied Thrash, then this is certainly worth picking up.<br /><br />*** If you should happen to buy the Special Edition version, you will get one card-sleeve housing two individual digipak cases. 0545403359|4.0|I admit that I only picked this up to read because of the Spielberg movie but I'm not sorry that I did. Albert's drunken father sells Joey to keep the family farm.  Joey suddenly goes from being a gently worked farm horse to a true war horse, being used to pull carts and artillery during heavy fighting.  His horror and surprise are evident in every sentence during the entire book and it doesn't take horse sense to see the absolute brutality man can inflict on both beast and human.  Joey's only friend is another horse, Tophorn, and he never gives up hope he might see Albert again one day.<br /><br />The story is told from the point of view of Joey and the sentences are written very short and terse.  Much of the book skips over entire periods of time but perhaps this is how horses think and talk?  The ending is a bit predictable but is still very sweet and a tear-jerker. I am intrigued by the idea of a classroom lesson: have the boys read War Horse and the girls read Black Beauty to discuss the stories from a gender point of view.

B005FNVDSA|4.0|Of course, there are many other better versions of the Brahms First Piano Concerto in the recording market. Even Maurizio Pollini himself, a decade ago, signed one which in my opinion has remained a landmark for the work's interpretation. That time, he was paired by a fabulous orchestra (Berlin Philharmonic) and a legendary conductor (Claudio Abbado). Although inevitable, comparisons are not the point of this commentary.<br /><br />Now, Pollini (almost 70) comes back to the beloved score and decides to re-record it this time in the company of the Dresden Staatskapelle (under Christian Thielemann, its new chief-conductor). Nothing wrong in his option, except the fact that - in technical terms - this new live CD takes the risk to be compared to Pollini's quite perfect version of late 1990s. When opposed to Dresdners, Berliners are definitely more supportive, more flexible and more prompt in giving the soloist the mellow atmosphere Brahms work requires. Not to speak about the recorded sound supplied by (the same!) DG! Now is not at the same qualitative level as the previous attempt used us. On the other hand, the sentimental significance of Pollini's gesture of coming back to a beloved stage, to a legendary orchestra and to a sensitive audience places by itself the outcome to a high valuable level.<br /><br />All in all, I think this new release is to be regarded merely as a memento marking the debut of a promising collaboration (Dresden - Thielemann) granted by a super star of the musical world (Maurizio Pollini). Pollini's performance = 5 stars, recording's technical conditions = 3 stars.

0062197258|5.0|Catherine Bailey still hasn't met Mr. Right, but she believed her luck might finally have turned when she met Lee Brightman. Four years later, she still hasn't recovered from the horrors she experienced at Lee's hands. Lee is serving a three year sentence after leaving her for dead and Catherine, now Cathy, is trying to make progress with each new day. Even days, odd days, cloudy days, each requires something different. Some days she can barely leave her apartment. Others, she's ok as long as she checks the doors and windows. Cathy needs to feel safe. But when Lee is released, Cathy knows that she may never feel safe again.<br /><br />Whoa! INTO THE DARKEST CORNER is dark and it's twisted, but once you start, you're not going to want to put this one down.<br /><br />Elizabeth Haynes's debut thriller is definitely a bit like Sleeping With the Enemy with a little twist. Cathy suffers from serious OCD and PTSD as a result of Lee's violence. Haynes alternates between Catherine at the beginning of - and through - her relationship with Lee and the three years later Cathy, making clear just how much she's changed. The girl who was once a partier with a horde of close friends becomes a loner who cringes at close contact. And as her situation worsens with Lee, it also becomes clear how much strength it's taken for her to survive the whole thing, pointing to an inevitable climactic ending that Haynes delivers 100%.
